=== Anuken@Mindustry.md ===
# Contributing
## Basic Guidelines
#### Use an IDE.
#### Always test your changes.
#### Do not make large changes before discussing them first.
## Style Guidelines
#### Follow the formatting guidelines.
#### Do not use incompatible Java features (java.util.function, java.awt).
#### Use `arc` collections and classes when possible.
#### Avoid boxed types (Integer, Boolean)
#### Do not allocate anything if possible.
#### Avoid bloated code and unnecessary getters/setters.
#### Do not create methods unless necessary.

=== CompSciLauren@awesome-git-hooks.md ===
# Contribution Guidelines
## Pull Requests
## Adding a New Git Hook
#[!/bin/bash or other shebang]
# Based on a hook from [title of source]
# Source: [https://www.website.com/]
#
# This sentence describes in simple terms what the git hook is actually doing.
#
# The hook should exit with non-zero status after issuing an appropriate
# message if it stops the [git command]. (If your script doesn't do this then you can remove this section)
#
# Requirements:
#   * Python 2/3 (whatever language the script is written in)
#
# To enable this hook, rename this file to "[type of git hook]".
## Adding Anything Else
## How to Contribute

### Releasing a new version to NPM
# (1) Update the Changelog, following format from previous versions
# and commit those changes independently of other updates
# (2) Run tests, lint, build published dir, update package.json
# (3) If all is well, publish the new version to the npm registry
# (4) Then, update github with the associated tag

#pragma once
#include <string>
#include "caf/example/my_class.hpp"
#include <iostream>
#define CAF_SUITE example.my_class    // name of this test suite
#include "caf/example/my_class.hpp"   // header-under-test
#include "caf/test/dsl.hpp"           // caf::test includes
#include <iostream>                   // standard includes
  #include <vector>
  #include <sys/types.h>
  #include "3rd/party.h"
  #include "caf/fwd.hpp"
  #include "caf/example.hpp" // header for this .cpp file
  #include "caf/config.hpp" // needed for #ifdef guards
  #include <algorithm>
  #ifdef CAF_WINDOWS
  #include <windows.h>
  #else
  #include <sys/socket.h>
  #endif
  #include "some/other/library.h"
  #include "caf/actor.hpp"

# Contribution Guide
## Reporting New Issues
## Submitting Code
### Pull Request Guide
# Create a new branch for development. The name of branch should be semantic, avoiding words like 'update' or 'tmp'. We suggest to use feature/xxx, if the modification is about to implement a new feature.
# Run the test after you finish your modification. Add new test cases or change old ones if you feel necessary
# If your modification pass the tests, congradulations it's time to push your work back to us. Notice that the commit message should be wirtten in the following format.
### Style Guide
### Commit Message Format

### Documentation Styleguide
#### Example
# Public: Disable the package with the given name.
#
# * `name`    The {String} name of the package to disable.
# * `options` (optional) The {Object} with disable options (default: {}):
#   * `trackTime`     A {Boolean}, `true` to track the amount of time taken.
#   * `ignoreErrors`  A {Boolean}, `true` to catch and ignore errors thrown.
# * `callback` The {Function} to call after the package has been disabled.
#
# Returns `undefined`.

# accepts `13` for v0.13, `14` for v0.14, and for versions 15+,

# switch to React 0.13
# switch to React 0.14
# switch to React 15
# switch to React 16
# switch to React 16.5

# build Enzyme locally upon save
# faster feedback for TDD

## Logging
# Enable the console logging handler and the file handler to
# write rotating log files under buck-out/log/buck-*.log in the
# project(s) being used.
# Log to buck-out/log/buck-*log.
# Write to disk all log messages not otherwise filtered by the top-level ".level"
# property.
# Ignore the environment and always write UTF-8 to files.
# Replace the default fugly multiline log formatter with a custom one.
# Rotate up to this many log files, then start deleting the oldest one.

=== fdorg@flashdevelop.md ===
# AppMan entries
# Coding style
##### Use spaces instead of tabs with a width of 4
##### Naming should be in English and clear
##### Use camelCase for private members and uppercase for public properties, methods and types:
##### Use types without explicit path:
##### Do not use extensive extra empty lines and keep the code clean, not like:
##### Use brackets and parenthesis for easier readability:
##### Do not nest expressions without brackets:
##### Use can use one liners to shorten the code:
##### Use explicit types:
##### Code example:
##### More generally, be consistent and keep the code clean!

=== forkcms@forkcms.md ===
# Contributing
## Guidelines
## Running Tests
# run all tests (so on an installed fork)
# only run unit tests (requires no database setup)
## How to submit pull requests
### Creating your own Fork
### Getting a local Fork instance
# Go to the directory where you want to store Fork, for example ~/Sites/forkcms
# Clone your version of Fork in the current directory (mind the dot at the end)
# If you get permission denied errors, read https://help.github.com/articles/generating-ssh-keys/#platform-all
# Install the dependencies of Fork CMS
# you will need composer: https://getcomposer.org/doc/00-intro.md#globally
### Creating a branch
# Create and go to a branch in one step!
# Create a new branch
# Go to this branch
### Work on your feature/bugfix
# Check what has changed in your branch
# Use this until all files you wish to commit have been added
# Use this to add all changed files to your commit
# Commit your changes
### Pushing your code to your Forked repository
# Push your code to the remote
### Submitting your pull request
### Waiting for approval
### Squashing commits
# squash the last 5 commits
# overwrite the git history on the remote too
## Support

### Git Commit Messages ###
### Documentation Styleguide ###
### Shell Styleguide ###
#### Function documentation ####
    #######################################
    # Cleanup files from the backup dir.
    #
    # Globals:
    #   VAR1 (RO,bool)    : `my_func` access to VAR1.
    #   VAR2 (WO)         : `my_func` change the value of VAR2.
    #   VAR3 (RW)         : `my_func` read and write to VAR3.
    # Arguments:
    #   arg1 ($1,int)     : Directory to cleanup.
    #   arg2 ($2-)        : Command to execute for the cleanup.
    # Returns:
    #   0                 : Cleanup completed successfully.
    #   101               : Backup directory is not readable.
    #   $NOT_DIR_ERROR    : Backup directory is not a directory.
    # Output:
    #   None
    #######################################

=== iptv-org@iptv.md ===
# Contributing Guide
## Add channel
#EXTINF:-1,Example TV
#EXTINF:-1 tvg-id="exampletv.us" tvg-name="Example TV" tvg-language="English" tvg-logo="http://example.com/channel-logo.png" group-title="News",Example TV
#EXTINF:-1 tvg-id="exampletv.us" tvg-name="Example TV" tvg-language="English" tvg-logo="http://example.com/channel-logo.png" group-title="News",Example TV
#EXTVLCOPT:http-referrer=http://example.com/
#EXTVLCOPT:http-user-agent=Mozilla/5.0 (Windows NT 10.0; Win64; x64)
## Add EPG source
#EXTM3U x-tvg-url="http://example.com/epg.xml.gz"
#EXTINF:-1 tvg-id="cnn" tvg-name="CNN",CNN
## Sort channels by category
#EXTINF:-1 group-title="News",CNN
## Sort channels by language
#EXTINF:-1 tvg-language="Arabic",Abu Dhabi Drama
#EXTINF:-1 tvg-language="English;Chinese",CCTV
## Sort channels by country
## Remove broken broadcasts

=== liip@LiipImagineBundle.md ===
# Contributing
## Request Feature
## Report Bug
## Submit Your Changes
   # after forking, clone your fork (replace <user> with your github username)
   # enter the newly cloned repository directory
   # EITHER checkout a "feature-<name>" branch if creating a new feature
   # OR checkout a "bugfix-<name>" branch if working on a bug fix
   # install required, default dependencies
   # install any optional dependencies, if required
   # stage your changed files or directories
   # commit your changes with a short descriptive message
   # run the test suite by calling simple-phpunit
    # call php-cs-fixer with "--dry-run" option to view changes without applying them
    # to apply the code style changes, run without the "--dry-run" option
    # commit any changes made by the tool
   # push your local changes to your remote fork
## Additional information

=== mapnik@mapnik.md ===
# Contributing
## Building Mapnik for development
## Testing
    # then go back to mapnik core
    # the submodule should be marked dirty
    # now commit the changes to the submodule
### Visual tests
#### Visual test style format
## Community
## Plugins
## Code Philosophy
## Code commits best practices.
#### Big changes - awesome as pull requests
#### Commits that fix issues should note the issue #
#### Commits that relate to issues should reference them:
#### Commits that add a new feature or fix should be added to the CHANGELOG
## License
## Copyright
## Coding Conventions
#### Prefix cmath functions with std::
#### Avoid boost::lexical_cast
#### Avoid sstream objects if possible
#### Spaces not tabs, and avoid trailing whitespace
#### Indentation is four spaces
#### Use C++ style casts
#### Use const keyword after the type
#### Pass built-in types by value, all others by const&
#### Use unique_ptr instead of new/delete
#### Use std::copy instead of memcpy
#### When to use shared_ptr and unique_ptr
#### Shared pointers should be created with [boost::make_shared](http://www.boost.org/doc/libs/1_47_0/libs/smart_ptr/make_shared.html) where possible
#### Use assignment operator for zero initialized numbers
#### Function definitions should not be separated from their arguments:
#### Separate arguments by a single space:
#### Space between operators:
#### Braces should always be used:
#### Braces should be on a separate line:
#### Prefer `empty()` over `size() == 0` if container supports it
### Other C++ style resources
### Emacs helper
### Generating *.gcov files with LLVM/clang toolchain to check tests coverage

## Contributing a patch
### Your first contribution / what can I help with?
### Code style and standards
### How do I make a pull request??
    # Run liquidprompt and check that your issue is still on that branch
    # Prepare a fix (include the issue number in the branch name if an issue
    # already exists)
    # Prepare a new feature
    # Hack, commit, hack, amend commit...
    # Fork the project on GitHub (if you haven't yet)
    # Add the remote target for pushes
    # Check that your local repo is up to date
    # Rebase your work on the latest state of `master`
    # Push your commits
    # Create the pull request on GitHub. Check that Github chose the `master`
    # branch as the starting point for your branch.
### How do I make a good pull request?

## Building and testing with other build systems
## Running the tests manually
    # This will run the Reader/Writer tests
    # This will run the Reader/Writer tests, using JSONChecker test suite
    # (http://www.json.org/JSON_checker/).
    # Notes: not all tests pass: JsonCpp is too lenient (for example,
    # it allows an integer to start with '0'). The goal is to improve
    # strict mode parsing to get all tests to pass.
    # This will run the unit tests (mostly Value)
    # You can run the tests using valgrind:

=== pnp@sp-dev-fx-webparts.md ===
# Contribution Guidance
## Code of Conduct
## Question or Problem?
## Typos, Issues, Bugs and contributions
## Sample Naming and Structure Guidelines
## Submitting Pull Requests
  # check if you have a remote pointing to the Microsoft repo:
  # if you see a pair of remotes (fetch & pull) that point to https://github.com/SharePoint/sp-dev-fx-webparts, you're ok... otherwise you need to add one
  # add a new remote named "upstream" and point to the Microsoft repo
    # assuming you are in the folder of your locally cloned fork....
    # assuming you have a remote named `upstream` pointing official **sp-dev-fx-webparts** repo
    # update your local master to be a mirror of what's in the main repo
    # switch to your branch where you are working, say "react-taxonomypicker"
    # update your branch to update it's fork point to the current tip of master & put your changes on top of it
## Merging your Existing GitHub Projects with this Repository
## Signing the CLA

=== preactjs@preact.md ===
# Contributing
## Getting Started
## The Repo Structure
# The repo root (folder where you cloned the repo into)
  # Sub-package, can be imported via `preact/compat` by users.
  # Compat stands for react-compatibility layer which tries to mirror the
  # react API as close as possible (mostly legacy APIs)
  # Sub-package, can be imported via `preact/hooks` by users.
  # The hooks API is an effect based API to deal with component lifcycles.
  # It's similar to hooks in React
  # Sub-package, can be imported via `preact/debug` by users.
  # Includes debugging warnings and error messages for common mistakes found
  # in Preact application. Also hosts the devtools bridge
  # Sub-package, can be imported via `preact/test-utils` by users.
  # Provides helpers to make testing Preact applications easier
  # A demo application that we use to debug tricky errors and play with new
  # features.
  # Contains build scripts and dependencies for development
### What does `mangle.json` do?
## What does `options.js` do?
## Important Branches
## Creating your first Pull-Request
## Commonly used scripts for contributions
## Common terminology and variable names
## Tips for getting to know the code base
## FAQ
### Why does the JSDoc use TypeScript syntax to specify types?
### Why does the code base often use `let` instead of `const`?
## How to create a good bug report
## I have more questions on how to contribute to Preact. How can I reach you?
## Releasing Preact (Maintainers only)
## Legacy Releases (8.x)

## Pull request
## How to open a pull request
# Go to a directory of your choice, where the qTox directory will be created:
# Clone the forked repo:
# Add the "upstream" remote to be able to fetch from the qTox upstream repository:
# Fetch from the "upstream" repository
# Point the local "master" branch to the "upstream" repository
# Fetch from the "upstream" repository:
# Checkout a local branch on up-to-date "master" and give it a sane name, e.g.:
# Push to the new upstream branch and link it for synchronization
# From now on, you can simply…
# ...to your brand new pull request.
## How to deal with large amounts of merge conflicts
# If not on PR branch, check it out:
# Now fetch master ALWAYS from upstream repo
# Last, rebase PR branch onto master…
# …and, if everything's clear, force push to YOUR repo (your "origin" Git remote)

#!/usr/bin/env bash
# Exit the script with a nonzero exit code if:
# * any individual command finishes with a nonzero exit code, or
# * we access any undefined variable.
# Invoke the general purpose predicate script that comes in the

#
# You'll need to replace `--whatever-flags` with things that are specific to the
# incorrectness you're trying to pin down. See below for details.

=== samuelcolvin@pydantic.md ===
## Issues
## Pull Requests
# 1. clone your fork and cd into the repo directory
# 2. Set up a virtualenv for running tests
# (or however you prefer to setup a python environment, 3.6 will work too)
# 3. Install pydantic, dependencies and test dependencies
# 4. Checkout a new branch and make your changes
# make your changes...
# 5. Fix formatting and imports
# Pydantic uses black to enforce formatting and isort to fix imports
# (https://github.com/ambv/black, https://github.com/timothycrosley/isort)
# 6. Run tests and linting
# there are a few sub-commands in Makefile like `test`, `testcov` and `lint`
# which you might want to use, but generally just `make` should be all you need
# 7. Build documentation
# if you have changed the documentation make sure it builds successfully
# you can also use `make docs-serve` to serve the documentation at localhost:8000
# ... commit, push, and create your pull request

=== simbody@simbody.md ===
### Mechanics of submitting a PR
### Basic requirements
#### Write new code in C++
#### Keep line width to 80 characters
#### Do not use tabs to indent; use 4 spaces
#### Use English and a spell checker
#### Provide Doxygen comments
#### Code should be `const` correct
#### Objects should be thread safe
### Naming conventions
#### Types: classes and structs, typedefs, enums
#### Constants
#### Functions and methods
#### Variables
#### Preprocessor macros
#### Namespaces
#### Header Guards
#ifndef SimTK_MODULE_SOME_CLASS_NAME_H_
#define SimTK_MODULE_SOME_CLASS_NAME_H_
#endif // SimTK_MODULE_SOME_CLASS_NAME_H_
#### Calendar dates
### C++ tips and style guide
#### Public class members come first
#### Use anonymous namespaces
#### Don't waste lines on curly braces
#### Throw and return are not functions
#### *Pre*fer *pre*-increment and *pre*-decrement operators
#### Place pointer and reference symbols with the type
#### Avoid spaces that don't improve readability
#### Make assignment operators safe for self-assignment

# TensorLayer Contributor Guideline
## Welcome to contribute!
## Checklist
## Continuous integration
## Build from sources
# First clone the repository and change the current directory to the newly cloned repository
# Install virtualenv if necessary
# Then create a virtualenv called `venv`
# Activate the virtualenv
## Linux:
## Windows:
# ============= IF TENSORFLOW IS NOT ALREADY INSTALLED ============= #
# basic installation
# advanced: for a machine **without** an NVIDIA GPU
# advanced: for a machine **with** an NVIDIA GPU
## Unittest
# install pytest
# run pytest
# install coverage
# For example: cd tests/layers/
# run unittest
# For example: coverage run --source tensorlayer.layers -m unittest discover
# generate html report
## Documentation
# then view generated local documentation by ./html/index.html
## General intro to TensorLayer2
# An example of a static model
# A static model has inputs and outputs with fixed shape.
# An example of a dynamic model
# A dynamic model has more flexibility. The inputs and outputs may be different in different runs.
    # a dynamic model allows more flexibility by customising forwarding.
## How to contribute a new `Layer`
